Hanafi Rulings on Kufr-Inducing Statements About Allah
Lists statements about Allah and worship that cause apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify statements and actions that constitute apostasy (kufr) according to the Hanafi school and classify the basis of each ruling (e.g., mockery, anthropomorphism, denial).

Core Idea
Many everyday words can nullify iman if they show contempt for Allah or His religion — intention matters but is not always a saving factor.

This lesson presents a comprehensive list of statements and actions that cause apostasy (kufr) according to the Hanafi school. These rulings are derived from later fatwa collections and reflect the school's thorough approach to protecting the sanctity of iman. Understanding these statements helps a Muslim guard his tongue and know the boundaries of lawful speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Category of Kufr
For each statement in the passage, determine the category of apostasy it falls under: anthropomorphism (tashbih), mockery (istihza'), denial of divine attributes, claiming knowledge of the unseen, disrespect towards prophets, etc.
The passage often begins with general principles before listing specific examples.
2
State the Specific Phrase
Extract the exact Arabic phrase (or its meaning) that triggers kufr. For example, 'بارك الله في كذبك' (May Allah bless your lie). Then note the ruling: does it cause kufr unconditionally or are there conditions?
Many phrases are followed by 'عند البعض' (according to some) or 'وعليه الفتوى' (fatwa is given accordingly).
3
Note Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Identify where there is disagreement within the Hanafi school. For instance, on saying 'لا أخاف الله' (I do not fear Allah), some say it is kufr only if there is no intent of mockery; others say it is always kufr. Note the preferred view ('على الأصح').
The author often resolves the ikhtilaf by stating the relied-upon position.
4
Determine the Underlying Principle
Ask: Why does this statement cause kufr? Common principles include: attributing deficiency to Allah (al-jahl, al-ajz), denying His attributes (e.g., knowledge of the unseen), showing contempt (istihza'), or associating partners (shirk).
The principle helps in analogizing new cases.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Hypothetical
Take a modern statement that resembles one from the list and test if it would be kufr according to the Hanafi criteria. For example, 'Allah is my witness that I didn't take the money' when knowing you did. This falls under false oath, which the passage implies is kufr (using Allah's name in false testimony).
This step simulates ifta practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيكفر إذا وصف الله تعالى بما لا يليق به أو سخر باسم من أسمائه أو بأمر من أوامره أو أنكر وعده أو وعيده أو جعل له شريكاً أو ولداً أو زوجة أو نسبه إلى الجهل أو العجز أو النقص. واختلفوا في قوله فلان في عيني كاليهودي في عين الله فكفره الجمهور، وقيل لا إن عنی به استقباح فعله، وقيل يكفر إن عنى الجارحة لا القدرة، والأصح مذهب المتقدمين في المتشابه كاليد، واختلفوا في جواز أن يقال بين يدي الله ويكفر بقوله يجوز أن يفعل الله فعلاً لا حكمة فيه وبإثبات المكان لله تعالى فإن قال الله في السماء فإن قصد حكاية ما جاء في اللفظة، وقيل تجوز فإنه قد جاء في الحديث أنه يوقف بين يدي الله تعالى على الصراط . قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني رحمه الله : هذا اللفظ موسع بالعربية والفارسية يطلق على الله تعالى وإن كان تعالى منزهاً عن الجهة وجوزه السرخسي أيضاً ومن يتحرز عن إطلاقه بالفارسية فإنما ذلك مخافة فتنة . ظاهر الأخبار لا يكفر، وإن أراد المكان كفر، وإن لم يكن له نية كفر عند الأكثر وهو الأصح وعليه الفتوى. ويكفر إن اعتقد أن الله تعالى يرضى بالكفر، وبقوله لو أنصفني الله تعالى يوم القيامة انتصفت منك، أو إن قضى الله يوم القيامة أو إذا أنصف الله، وبقوله بارك الله في كذبك، وبقوله الله جلس للإنصاف أو قام له وبقوله هذا لا يمرض هذا ممن نسيه الله أو على الأصح وبوصفه تعالى بالفوق أو بالتحت وبظنه أن الجنة وما فيها للفناء عند البعض، وبقوله لامرأته أنت أحب إلي من الله وقيل لا، وبقوله لا أخاف الله أو لا أخشاه عند البعض ومحل الاختلاف عند عدم قصد الاستهزاء، وبقولها لا جواباً لقوله أما تعرفين الله على الظاهر، وبقوله لا أريد اليمين بالله وإنما أريد اليمين بالطلاق أو بالعتاق عند البعض خلافاً للعامة وهو الأصح وبقوله رأيت الله في المنام، وبقوله المعدوم ليس بمعلوم لله تعالى، وبقول الظالم أنا أفعل بغير تقدير الله تعالى، وبإدخاله الكاف في آخر الله عند ندائه عبد الله وإن كان عالماً على الأصح ، وبتصغير الخالق عمداً عالماً، وبقوله ليتني لم أسلم إلى هذا الوقت حتى أرث أبي وبقوله إن كنت فعلت كذا أمس فهو كافر وهو يعلم أنه قد فعله إذا كان عنده أنه يكفر به وعليه الفتوى وبقوله الله يعلم أني فعلت كذا وهو يعلم أنه ما فعل عند العامة إن كان اختياراً لا مخافة وبقوله إن كنت قلته فأنا كافر وهو يعلم أنه قاله، وبقوله بريء من الله لولا ولم يتم تعليقه خلافاً للبعض قياساً على أنت طالق ثلاثاً لولا لم يقع، وبقولها نعم جواباً لقوله أتعلمين الغيب وبتزوجه بشهادة الله ورسوله، وبقوله فلان يموت بهذا المرض عند البعض، وبقوله عند رقاء الهامة يموت أحد عند البعض والأصح . وبقوله عند رؤية الدائرة التي تكون حول القمر يكون مطر مدعياً علم الغيب، وبرجوعه من سفره عند سماع صياح العقعق عند البعض، وبإتيان الكاهن وتصديقه، وبقوله أنا أعلم المسروقات، وبقوله أنا أخبر عن أخبار الجن إياي وبعدم الإقرار ببعض الأنبياء عليهم السلام أو عيبه نبياً بشيء أو عدم الرضا بسنة من سنن المرسلين، وبقوله لا أعلم أن آدم عليه السلام نبي أولا، ولو قال آمنت الأنبياء عليهم السلام وبعدم معرفة أن محمداً بجميع آخر الأنبياء عند البعض وبنسبته نبياً إلى الفواحش كعزمه على الزنا وقيل لا، وبقوله إن الأنبياء عصو وإن كان معصية كفر ، وبقوله لم تعص الأنبياء حال النبوة وقبلها لرده النصوص لا بقوله لا أقبل شفاعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الإمهال فكيف أقبلها منك ، ولا بأنكاره نبوة الخضر وذي الكفل عليهما السلام لعدم الإجماع على نبوتهما، ويكفر من أراد بغض النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بقلبه وبقوله لو كان فلان نبياً لا أؤمن به لا بقوله لو كان صهري رسول الله لا أئتمر بأمره، ويكفر بقوله إن كان ما قال الأنبياء حقاً أو صدقاً، وبقوله أنا رسول الله وبطلبه المعجزة حين ادعى الجهال فأما من حيث الدين فلا بأس به .
He becomes a kafir if he describes Allah with what does not befit Him, or mocks any of His names or commands, or denies His promise or threat, or assigns to Him a partner, child, or spouse, or attributes ignorance, incapacity, or deficiency to Him. They differed on his saying 'So-and-so is in my eye like a Jew in Allah's eye': the majority held it as kufr; it is said no if he meant disapproval of his action; it is said he becomes a kafir if he meant the organ not power; the correct view is the way of the early scholars regarding ambiguous verses like 'the hand'. They differed on the permissibility of saying 'between the hands of Allah'; he becomes a kafir by saying 'Allah may do an action with no wisdom in it' or by affirming a place for Allah. If he says 'Allah is in the heaven', if he intends to relate what is reported in the phrase, the apparent narrations say he does not become a kafir; if he intends place, he becomes a kafir; if he has no intention, he becomes kafir according to most, which is the correct view and fatwa is given accordingly. He becomes a kafir if he believes that Allah is pleased with kufr, or by saying 'If Allah were just to me on the Day of Judgment, I would get my right from you', or 'If Allah decrees on the Day of Judgment', or 'When Allah does justice', or by saying 'May Allah bless your lie', or 'Allah sat down for justice' or 'stood up for it', or by saying 'This one who does not get sick, this is one whom Allah has forgotten' or on the correct view. And by describing Allah with 'above' or 'below', and by his assumption that Paradise and what is in it will perish according to some, and by his saying to his wife 'You are more beloved to me than Allah' — and it is said no. And by his saying 'I do not fear Allah' or 'I do not dread Allah' according to some — and the place of difference is when there is no intent of mockery. And by her saying 'Yes' in answer to his saying 'Do you not know Allah?' according to the apparent view. And by his saying 'I do not want to swear by Allah, rather I want to swear by divorce or by emancipation' according to some, contrary to the general scholars, and this is the correct view. And by his saying 'I saw Allah in a dream'. And by his saying 'The nonexistent is not known to Allah'. And by the oppressor's saying 'I do things without Allah's decree'. And by his inserting 'kaf' at the end of Allah when calling 'Abdullah' even if he is knowledgeable, on the correct view. And by deliberately and knowingly using the diminutive of 'al-Khaliq'. And by his saying 'Would that I had not accepted Islam until now so that I could inherit from my father.' And by his saying 'If I did such-and-such yesterday, then I am a kafir' knowing that he did it, if in his view that action makes him a kafir — and fatwa is given accordingly. And by his saying 'Allah knows that I did such-and-such' while knowing he did not do it, according to the general scholars, if it was by choice not fear. And by his saying 'If I said it, then I am a kafir' while knowing he said it. And by his saying 'I am free of Allah, if not...' without completing the conditional, contrary to some, by analogy with 'You are thrice divorced, if not' which does not occur. And by her saying 'Yes' in answer to his saying 'Do you know the unseen?' And by his marrying with the testimony of Allah and His Messenger. And by his saying 'So-and-so will die from this illness' according to some. And by his saying at the appearance of the owl 'One of us will die' according to some — and the correct view. And by his saying upon seeing the ring around the moon 'There will be rain', claiming knowledge of the unseen. And by his returning from his journey upon hearing the cawing of a crow according to some. And by going to a soothsayer and believing him. And by his saying 'I know the locations of stolen goods.' And by his saying 'I am informed by the jinn.' And by not affirming some of the prophets (peace be upon them) or criticizing a prophet in any way, or not being pleased with any sunnah of the messengers. And by his saying 'I do not know if Adam (peace be upon him) was a prophet or not.' And if he says 'I believed in the prophets (peace be upon them)' but without knowing that Muhammad is the last of the prophets according to some. And by attributing a prophet to lewdness, like being determined to commit adultery — and it is said no. And by his saying 'The prophets sinned' even if it is a sin, it is kufr. And by his saying 'The prophets did not sin during prophethood or before it' because this is rejecting texts; not so if he says 'I do not accept the Prophet's intercession for postponement, so how can I accept it from you?'. And not by denying the prophethood of al-Khidr and Dhul-Kifl (peace be upon them) due to lack of consensus on their prophethood. And he becomes a kafir if he intends hatred of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his heart, and by his saying 'If so-and-so were a prophet, I would not believe in him' — not so by his saying 'If my brother-in-law were the Messenger of Allah, I would not obey his command.' And he becomes a kafir by saying 'If what the prophets said is true' or 'truthful', and by his saying 'I am a messenger of Allah' and by his requesting a miracle when he claims prophethood among the ignorant. As for the religious aspect, there is no harm in it.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive list of statements and beliefs that constitute apostasy (kufr) according to the Hanafi school. It begins with general principles: describing Allah improperly, mocking His names or commands, denying His promises, associating partners, etc. Then it delves into specific phrases and their rulings, often noting differences of opinion within the madhhab (e.g., 'فلان في عيني كاليهودي في عين الله', the majority say it is kufr, but some distinguish based on intent). It discusses anthropomorphic expressions like 'hand' and 'between the hands of Allah', following the approach of the early scholars (tafwid or ta'wil). It emphasizes that attributing direction or place to Allah is kufr, with detailed rulings on 'Allah is in the heaven'. The list continues with many examples: believing Allah is pleased with kufr, complaining about Allah's justice, saying 'May Allah bless your lie', suggesting Allah sits or stands, forgetting, describing Allah as 'above', claiming Paradise is perishable, preferring anyone above Allah in love, saying one does not fear Allah, answering affirmatively to 'Do you not know Allah?', preferring swearing by talaq over Allah, claiming to see Allah in a dream, saying the nonexistent is unknown to Allah, denying divine decree, altering Allah's name disrespectfully, using diminutive of al-Khaliq, regretting being Muslim to inherit, conditional self-declarations of kufr with knowledge, claiming to know the unseen through omens, consulting soothsayers, claiming knowledge from jinn, denying prophets or criticizing them, not knowing basic prophetic facts, attributing sins to prophets, rejecting intercession, the difference between hating the Prophet and merely not obeying a specific relative, and false claims of prophethood. The key is that most of these indicate either contempt for religion, denial of fundamental beliefs, or arrogating divine prerogatives (like knowledge of the unseen). The passage reflects the Hanafi method of enumerating specific causes of apostasy based on fatwa collections, with careful attention to intention and context.

Key Terms
كفر (kufr): Apostasy from Islam, nullifying marriage and requiring execution if not repented.
عناد (inad): Stubborn rejection after knowing the truth; one form of kufr.
استهزاء (istihza'): Mockery; causing kufr regardless of belief in the heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on someone who says 'بارك الله في كذبك' (May Allah bless your lie) knowing it is a lie?
A) He becomes a kafir because it is mockery of Allah's blessing.
B) He does not become a kafir because blessing a lie is not directly about Allah.
C) It is a sin but not apostasy.
D) It depends on his intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers a wide range of statements as apostasy to protect the inviolability of tawhid and respect for Allah, with a strong emphasis on avoiding any expression that diminishes reverence for the Divine.

Utterances That Cause Apostasy: The Hanafi Rulings
List of statements about Allah that cause apostasy with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between utterances that cause apostasy outright and those that depend on intent, and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling for each.

Core Idea
Many words about Allah are apostasy regardless of intention; for others, intent matters.

The Hanafi school provides a crucial distinction: some statements about Allah are so clearly indicative of disbelief that they cause apostasy without needing to consider the speaker's intention. Others are ambiguous and require examining the speaker's intent. This lesson walks you through the key categories and rulings from the classical text, focusing on the relied-upon positions (mufta bihi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage opens with a principle: 'zahir al-akhbar' (apparent news) does not cause disbelief unless the speaker intended place for Allah. This sets the stage for distinguishing between explicit and ambiguous utterances.
This principle is foundational: ambiguous statements require intent analysis.
2
List utterances that cause apostasy regardless of intent
Scan the passage for utterances listed without any condition or qualification. These include saying 'If Allah would judge fairly', 'May Allah bless your lie', describing Allah with spatial attributes, assuming Paradise will perish, preferring a human over Allah, etc.
These are explicit kufr; no need to ask about intent.
3
Identify utterances with divergent opinions
Some utterances have ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) mentioned. Examples: saying 'I do not fear Allah', 'I do not want to swear by Allah', 'You are more beloved to me than Allah', and conditional statements like 'If I did X, then I am a disbeliever'.
The text often indicates the most correct view (al-ashah) or the relied-upon position (alayhi al-fatwa).
4
Understand the role of intent
For some disputed cases, the text explicitly says the ikhtilaf is when there is no intention of mockery (e.g., 'I do not fear Allah'). If mockery is intended, all agree it is kufr.
Intent is only relevant for these specific ambiguous utterances.
5
Memorize the relied-upon positions
The passage concludes many entries with 'wa huwa al-ashah' or 'wa alayhi al-fatwa'. These are the operative rulings for fatwa. Focus on these for practical application.
Examples: the mufta bihi on 'You are more beloved than Allah' is that it is kufr; on 'I do not want to swear by Allah' it is kufr contrary to the general public.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظاهر الأخبار لا يكفر، وإن أراد المكان كفر، وإن لم يكن له نية كفر عند الأكثر وهو الأصح وعليه الفتوى. ويكفر إن اعتقد أن الله تعالى يرضى بالكفر، وبقوله لو أنصفني الله تعالى يوم القيامة انتصفت منك، أو إن قضى الله يوم القيامة أو إذا أنصف الله، وبقوله بارك الله في كذبك، وبقوله الله جلس للإنصاف أو قام له وبقوله هذا لا يمرض هذا ممن نسيه الله أو على الأصح وبوصفه تعالى بالفوق أو بالتحت وبظنه أن الجنة وما فيها للفناء عند البعض، وبقوله لامرأته أنت أحب إلي من الله وقيل لا، وبقوله لا أخاف الله أو لا أخشاه عند البعض ومحل الاختلاف عند عدم قصد الاستهزاء، وبقولها لا جواباً لقوله أما تعرفين الله على الظاهر، وبقوله لا أريد اليمين بالله وإنما أريد اليمين بالطلاق أو بالعتاق عند البعض خلافاً للعامة وهو الأصح وبقوله رأيت الله في المنام، وبقوله المعدوم ليس بمعلوم الله تعالى، وبقول الظالم أنا أفعل بغير تقدير الله تعالى، وبإدخاله الكاف في آخر الله عند ندائه عبد الله وإن كان عالماً على الأصح، وبتصغير الخالق عمداً عالماً، وبقوله ليتني لم أسلم إلى هذا الوقت حتى أرث أبي وبقوله إن كنت فعلت كذا أمس فهو كافر وهو يعلم أنه قد فعله إذا كان عنده أنه يكفر به وعليه الفتوى وبقوله الله يعلم أني فعلت كذا وهو يعلم أنه ما فعل عند العامة إن كان اختياراً لا مخافة وبقوله إن كنت قلته فأنا كافر وهو يعلم أنه قاله، وبقوله بريء من الله لولا ولم يتم تعليقه خلافاً للبعض قياساً على أنت طالق ثلاثاً لولا لم يقع.
The apparent news does not cause disbelief, but if he intended the place, he disbelieves; if he had no intention, he disbelieves according to the majority, which is the most correct, and upon it is the fatwa. And he disbelieves if he believes that Allah the Exalted is pleased with disbelief, and by his saying: 'If Allah the Exalted would have judged fairly between me and you on the Day of Judgment,' or 'If Allah judges on the Day of Judgment' or 'When Allah judges fairly,' and by his saying: 'May Allah bless your lie,' and by his saying: 'Allah sat for justice' or 'stood for it,' and by his saying: 'This one does not get sick; this is among those Allah has forgotten' or according to the most correct, and by describing the Exalted with above or below, and by his assumption that Paradise and what is in it will perish according to some, and by his saying to his wife: 'You are more beloved to me than Allah,' and it was said no, and by his saying: 'I do not fear Allah' or 'I do not stand in awe of Allah' according to some, and the place of difference is when there is no intention of mockery, and by her saying 'no' in response to his saying 'Do you not know Allah' apparently, and by his saying: 'I do not want to swear by Allah, but I want to swear by divorce or by emancipation' according to some, contrary to the general scholars, and it is the most correct, and by his saying: 'I saw Allah in a dream,' and by his saying: 'The non-existent is not known to Allah the Exalted,' and by the oppressor's saying: 'I do without the decree of Allah the Exalted,' and by his inserting the letter 'kaf' at the end of Allah when calling 'Abdallah' even if he is knowledgeable, according to the most correct, and by deliberately and knowingly making the Creator a diminutive, and by his saying: 'Would that I had not embraced Islam until this time so that I could inherit my father,' and by his saying: 'If I did such and such yesterday, then he is a disbeliever' while knowing that he did it if he thought that it constitutes disbelief, and upon it is the fatwa, and by his saying: 'Allah knows that I did such and such' while knowing that he did not do it, according to the general scholars if it was by choice and not out of fear, and by his saying: 'If I said it, then I am a disbeliever' while knowing that he said it, and by his saying: 'I am free from Allah, if not' and he did not complete the conditional statement, contrary to some, by analogy to 'You are divorced three times if not' which does not occur.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a listing of various utterances and beliefs that, according to Hanafi jurisprudence, constitute apostasy (riddah). The author begins with a general principle: if a person utters words that apparently indicate disbelief (kufr), the ruling depends on intention. If the person intended to attribute a location to Allah (which is impossible for Allah), he becomes an apostate. If he had no specific intention, the majority of scholars rule that he still becomes an apostate, and this is the relied-upon position. Then the author enumerates specific statements that cause apostasy, such as saying that Allah would judge unfairly on the Day of Judgment, blessing a lie, ascribing physical attributes to Allah like sitting or standing, describing Allah as being in a direction, assuming Paradise will perish, preferring a created being over Allah, claiming not to fear Allah, refusing to swear by Allah, claiming to see Allah in a dream (which is impossible in this world), denying that Allah knows non-existent things, doing acts without Allah's decree, adding a 'kaf' to Allah's name when calling 'Abdallah' (making it 'Abdallakah'), using the diminutive form for the Creator, regretting embracing Islam for worldly gains, and making conditional statements that imply disbelief. The author notes differences of opinion on some of these, but often concludes with 'al-ashah' (most correct) or 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' (and upon it is the fatwa). For example, regarding saying 'You are more beloved to me than Allah,' some say it is not kufr, but the correct view is that it is. Regarding saying 'I do not fear Allah,' the difference is when there is no intention of mockery. Similarly, the ruling on saying 'I do not want to swear by Allah' is that it is kufr according to some, but the general scholars disagree; the correct view is that it is kufr. The passage emphasizes that intent and context play a role in determining apostasy, but many statements are considered disbelief outright.

Key Terms
ظاهر الأخبار (zahir al-akhbar): Utterances that apparently seem to indicate disbelief but are ambiguous
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The authoritative legal ruling that is relied upon for issuing fatwas
الأصح (al-ashah): The most sound opinion among multiple narrations within the school

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person says 'You are more beloved to me than Allah' with no intention of mockery, what is the ruling?
A) He does not become an apostate.
B) He becomes an apostate.
C) It is makruh tanzihi.
D) It depends on his belief in Allah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, many utterances about Allah are considered apostasy regardless of intent, but for some, the speaker's intention is decisive, and the relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions are those stated in the text.

Rulings on Statements About the Prophet's Person
Disputed rulings on statements about the Prophet's person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for each of five statements about the Prophet's physical attributes and mental state, distinguishing between kufr and non-kufr based on intent.

Core Idea
Intent determines whether a statement about the Prophet is kufr or not.

The Hanafi school carefully examines the wording and intent of statements about the Prophet's person. This lesson covers five scenarios: using a diminutive for the Prophet's hair, doubting his humanity, insulting a namesake, compelled insult, and attributing insanity or fainting. In each case, the ruling hinges on whether the speaker intended disrespect (istikhfaf) or veneration (ta'dhim).

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement
Read each phrase beginning with 'بقوله' and identify the exact wording and context (e.g., diminutive, doubt, insult).
2
Determine the intent
The text explicitly links ruling to intent: if the speaker intended disrespect (إهانة), it is kufr; if veneration (تعظيم), it is not. For some statements, intent is inherent (e.g., doubting humanity).
3
Apply the ruling
State the ruling: kufr or not, based on the stated or presumed intent. Where there is ikhtilaf (dispute), note the differing views.
e.g., for the diminutive, the text says they differed; the later commentary clarifies the intent-based rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في تصغيره شعر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا إذا أراد الإهانة فيكفر أما إذا أراد التعظيم فلا، وبقوله لا أدري أكان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إنسياً أو جنياً، وبشتمه رجلاً اسمه محمد وكنيته أبو القاسم ذاكراً للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عند البعض، وبشتمه محمداً حين أكره على شتمه قائلاً قصدته، وبقوله جن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ساعة لا بقوله أغمي عليه. واختلفوا فيمن قال لو لم يأكل آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام الحنطة ما صرنا أشقياء، وبرده حديثاً مروياً إن كان متواتراً أو قال على وجه الاستخفاف سمعناه كثيراً، وبتمنيه أن لا يكون بعض الأنبياء نبياً مريداً به الاستخفاف به أو عداوته لا بقوله لو لم يبعث الله نبياً لم يكن خارجاً عن الحكمة، وبقوله أنا لا أحبه حين قيل له إن النبي لو كان يحب القرع وقيل إن كان على وجه الإهانة، وبقولها نعم حين قال لها لو شهد عندك الأنبياء والملائكة لا تصدقيهم حين قالت له لا تكذب وباستخفافه بسنة من السنن وبقوله لا أدري أن النبي في القبر مؤمن أم كافر، وبقوله ما كان علينا نعمة من النبي عليه السلام لأن البعثة من أعظم النعم،
And they differed regarding his making the hair of the Prophet, peace be upon him, into a diminutive: unless he intended insult, then he disbelieves; but if he intended veneration, then not. And by his saying 'I do not know whether the Prophet, peace be upon him, was human or jinn.' And by his insulting a man named Muhammad whose kunya is Abu al-Qasim, intending the Prophet, peace be upon him, according to some. And by his insulting Muhammad when compelled to insult him, saying 'I intended him.' And by his saying 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, became insane for an hour,' not by his saying 'He fainted.' And they differed regarding one who said 'If Adam, peace be upon him, had not eaten the wheat, we would not have become miserable.' And by his rejecting a narrated hadith if it is mutawatir or if he said it derisively 'We heard it often.' And by his wishing that some prophet were not a prophet, intending mockery or enmity, not by his saying 'If Allah had not sent a prophet, it would not be outside wisdom.' And by his saying 'I do not love him' when it was said to him 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to like pumpkins,' and it was said if it was insulting. And by her saying 'yes' when he said to her 'If the prophets and angels testify for you, I would not believe them' while she told him 'Do not lie.' And by his making light of a Sunnah. And by his saying 'I do not know whether the Prophet is in the grave a believer or a disbeliever.' And by his saying 'We have no blessing from the Prophet, peace be upon him,' because the sending of the Prophet is among the greatest blessings.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage addresses several disputed points regarding apostasy. First, regarding using a diminutive form for the hair of the Prophet (e.g., 'shu'ayra' instead of 'sha'r'): if done disrespectfully, it is kufr; if done to show veneration (ta'dhim), it is not. Then, saying he does not know whether the Prophet was human or jinn is kufr because it doubts his humanity. Insulting a person named Muhammad with the kunya Abu al-Qasim while intending the Prophet is kufr; if forced to insult the Prophet, saying 'I intended him' (i.e., the person) might exempt him. Saying the Prophet became insane (jun) for a moment is kufr, but saying he fainted is not. Regarding the statement about Adam and the wheat (referring to the story of Adam eating from the tree): this is a disputed matter; the text does not give a definitive ruling here but notes the difference. Rejecting a mutawatir hadith or saying it derisively is kufr. Wishing a prophet were not a prophet with mockery or enmity is kufr, but saying 'If Allah had not sent a prophet, it would not be outside wisdom' is not necessarily kufr. Saying 'I do not love him' about the Prophet if the context is insulting is kufr. Telling one's wife that he would not believe her even if prophets testify, when she says 'do not lie,' is kufr. Making light of any Sunnah is kufr. Saying 'I do not know whether the Prophet is a believer or disbeliever in the grave' is kufr because it doubts his faith. Saying 'We have no blessing from the Prophet' is kufr because his prophethood is the greatest blessing. The passage illustrates that in matters of apostasy, the Hanafi school carefully analyzes the intent and context of statements, with differences of opinion on borderline cases.

Key Terms
التصغير (al-tasghir): Using the diminutive form for something associated with the Prophet, e.g., 'shu'ayra' instead of 'sha'r'.
الاستخفاف (al-istikhfaf): Making light of or mocking religious matters, a key factor in apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone uses a diminutive for the Prophet's hair with the intention of veneration?
A) He becomes an apostate.
B) He does not become an apostate.
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is haram but not kufr.

Key Takeaway
Intent separates kufr from permissible speech when the same words can be used respectfully or disrespectfully.

Rulings on Statements About Prophets and Rejecting Revelation
Disputed rulings on statements about prophets and revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on four statements regarding prophets and revelation: the Adam story, rejecting mutawatir hadith, wishing a prophet were not a prophet, and denying blessing from the Prophet.

Core Idea
Rejecting revelation or belittling any prophet is kufr; intent matters in some cases.

This lesson covers statements that touch on the status of prophets and the authority of revelation. The Hanafi school rulings on blaming Adam for misery, rejecting a mutawatir hadith, wishing a prophet did not exist, and denying the Prophet's blessing all relate to undermining faith. The lesson clarifies where kufr occurs and where it does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement
Read each phrase: blaming Adam, rejecting hadith, wishing a prophet were not, denying blessing.
2
Check the type of evidence involved
For rejecting hadith, determine if it is mutawatir or not. For wishing, determine if it is mockery or a hypothetical. For blessing, recognize it as a necessary belief.
3
Apply the ruling
The text gives explicit rulings: blaming Adam is disputed; rejecting mutawatir is kufr; wishing with mockery is kufr; denying blessing is kufr. Note the exceptions.

Commentary
This passage addresses several disputed points regarding apostasy. First, regarding using a diminutive form for the hair of the Prophet (e.g., 'shu'ayra' instead of 'sha'r'): if done disrespectfully, it is kufr; if done to show veneration (ta'dhim), it is not. Then, saying he does not know whether the Prophet was human or jinn is kufr because it doubts his humanity. Insulting a person named Muhammad with the kunya Abu al-Qasim while intending the Prophet is kufr; if forced to insult the Prophet, saying 'I intended him' (i.e., the person) might exempt him. Saying the Prophet became insane (jun) for a moment is kufr, but saying he fainted is not. Regarding the statement about Adam and the wheat (referring to the story of Adam eating from the tree): this is a disputed matter; the text does not give a definitive ruling here but notes the difference. Rejecting a mutawatir hadith or saying it derisively is kufr. Wishing a prophet were not a prophet with mockery or enmity is kufr, but saying 'If Allah had not sent a prophet, it would not be outside wisdom' is not necessarily kufr. Saying 'I do not love him' about the Prophet if the context is insulting is kufr. Telling one's wife that he would not believe her even if prophets testify, when she says 'do not lie,' is kufr. Making light of any Sunnah is kufr. Saying 'I do not know whether the Prophet is a believer or disbeliever in the grave' is kufr because it doubts his faith. Saying 'We have no blessing from the Prophet' is kufr because his prophethood is the greatest blessing. The passage illustrates that in matters of apostasy, the Hanafi school carefully analyzes the intent and context of statements, with differences of opinion on borderline cases.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A hadith transmitted by so many narrators that it is impossible they conspired to lie.
الاستخفاف (al-istikhfaf): Making light of or mocking religious matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on saying 'We have no blessing from the Prophet'?
A) It is kufr because the Prophet's mission is the greatest blessing.
B) It is not kufr because it is a matter of personal opinion.
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is disputed.

Key Takeaway
Rejecting revelation or belittling a prophet is generally kufr, but hypothetical statements about divine wisdom are not.

Rulings on Contextual Statements: Disbelief in Testimony, Love, Sunnah, and Faith
Rulings on contextual statements implying disrespect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on four contextual statements: saying 'I do not love him' about the Prophet, disbelieving a wife's testimony even with prophets, making light of a Sunnah, and doubting the Prophet's faith in the grave.

Core Idea
Statements that undermine the Prophet's honor or the authority of the Sunnah are kufr, regardless of intent in some cases.

This lesson covers statements that may appear less direct but still constitute apostasy. The Hanafi school rules that saying 'I do not love him' about the Prophet if insulting, disbelieving one's spouse even if prophets testify, making light of any Sunnah, and expressing doubt about the Prophet's faith in the grave are all kufr. These rulings emphasize the seriousness of maintaining respect for the Prophet and the religion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement and its context
Read each scenario: the love statement is linked to the Prophet's liking of pumpkins; the testimony statement is a reply to a wife; the sunnah statement is general; the grave statement doubts the Prophet's faith.
2
Determine if the statement implies disrespect or doubt
For 'I do not love him' consider if it was said in response to the Prophet's sunnah. For the testimony, consider that it implies the Prophet's testimony is not credible. For sunnah, any making light is kufr. For the grave, it doubts the Prophet's Islam.
3
Apply the ruling
All four are kufr according to the text. Note that for 'I do not love him,' it is kufr if it was intended as disrespect.

Miscellaneous Rulings on Apostasy
Various statements and actions that cause apostasy with some exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which statements and actions cause apostasy (kufr) in Hanafi fiqh and distinguish them from mere sins or mistakes, applying the principles of denail of daruriyyat and istihlal.

Core Idea
Apostasy occurs by explicit denial of daruriyyat or by istihlal of a known prohibition, not by mere sin.

This lesson covers a wide range of sayings and deeds that remove a person from Islam according to the Hanafi school. Some are overt denials of core beliefs, while others are conditional statements implying rebellion against Allah. You will learn to spot the difference between apostasy and mere error, and understand the crucial distinction between considering something halal (istihlal) and merely committing a sin.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the statement or action
First, identify whether the statement/action falls under denial of a daruri (necessarily known matter), istihlal of a known haram, conditional rebellion against Allah's command, or mocking religion.
Daruriyyat include the prophethood of Muhammad, the obligation of prayer, the prohibition of adultery, etc.
2
Check for exceptions
Some statements appear problematic but are ruled not kufr due to context or because they do not reach the level of denial. For example, saying 'I have not even a handspan in Paradise' due to humility, or denying 'ushr/kharaj in modern times.
Pay attention to phrases like 'على الأصح' (the most correct) and 'خلافاً لما عن' (contrary to what is transmitted from).
3
Apply the principle of istihlal vs mere action
Distinguish between actually considering a haram to be halal (istihlal) which is kufr, and merely committing the haram while still believing it is prohibited, which is a major sin but not apostasy.
The fatwa is on this view, contrary to certain narrations from Imam Muhammad and Abu Hafs.
4
Identify the hukm for each item
For each item in the passage, state whether it is kufr (apostasy) or not, and if not, what the correct classification is (e.g., mistake, major sin).
The passage explicitly marks some as 'يكفر' (he becomes a kafir) and others as 'لا يكفر' (he does not become a kafir).
5
Summarize the key categories
Group the causes of apostasy into: (1) Denial of Daruriyyat, (2) Istihlal, (3) Conditional rebellion, (4) Mocking religion/scholars. Group the non-causes into: (1) Mere error, (2) Statements of humility, (3) Contextual refusals (e.g., wife rejecting husband's command).
This step reinforces the overall structure of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقذفه عائشة رضي الله عنها من نسائه فقط، وبإنكاره صحبة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه بخلاف غيره، وبإنكاره إمامة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه على الأصح كإنكاره خلافة عمر رضي الله عنه على الأصح لا بقوله لولا نبينا لم يخلق آدم عليه السلام وهو خطأ، ويكفر بقوله لو أمرني الله بكذا لم أفعل، ولو صارت القبلة إلى هذه الجهة ما صليت، أو لو أعطاني الله الجنة لا أريدها دونك أو لا أدخلها مع فلان، أو لو أعطاني الله الجنة لأجلك أو لأجل هذا العمل لا أريدها وأريد رؤيته، وبقوله لا أترك النقد لأجل النسيئة جواباً لقوله دع الدنيا للآخرة، وبقوله لو أمرني الله بالزكاة أكثر من خمسة دراهم أو بالصوم أكثر من شهر لا أفعل، وبقوله الإيمان يزيد وينقص، وبقوله لا أدري الكافر في الجنة أو في النار أو لا أدري أين يصير الكافر، ويقتل بقوله أنا العن المذهبين جواباً لقوله على أي المذهبين أنت أبي حنيفة أو الشافعي وإن تاب عزر، ويكفر بإنكاره أصل الوتر والأضحية وباستحلال وطء الحائض لا بقوله ليس لي موضع شبر في الجنة لاستقلاله العمل ولا بقوله لا تكتب الحفظة على هذا الرجل. ولا بقوله هذا مكان لا إله فيه ولا رسول إلا إذا قصد به إنكار الدين، ولا بقول المرأة لا أتعلم ولا أصلي جواباً لقول الزوج تعلمي، ولا بإنكار العشر أو الخراج ولا يفسق خصوصاً في هذا الزمان، ولا بقوله من أكل حراماً فقد أكل ما رزقه الله لكنه أثم ويكفر باستحلاله حراماً علمت حرمته من الدين من غير ضرورة لا بفعله من غير استخلال خلافاً لما عن محمد رحمه الله في أكل الخنزير ولما عن أبي حفص في الخمر والفتوى على الأول، ويكفر بقوله للقبيح إنه...
And by his slandering Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, specifically from among his wives. And by his denying the companionship of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, unlike others. And by his denying the caliphate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, according to the most correct, like his denying the caliphate of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, according to the most correct, not by his saying 'Were it not for our Prophet, Adam would not have been created,' and it is a mistake. And he becomes an apostate by his saying 'If Allah commanded me to do such-and-such, I would not do it,' or 'If the qibla were in this direction, I would not pray,' or 'If Allah gave me Paradise, I would not want it without you,' or 'I would not enter it with so-and-so,' or 'If Allah gave me Paradise for your sake or for this deed, I do not want it, I want to see Him,' and by his saying 'I will not abandon criticism for the sake of deferment' in response to 'Leave this world for the hereafter,' and by his saying 'If Allah commanded me to give more than five dirhams in zakat or to fast more than a month, I would not do it,' and by his saying 'Faith increases and decreases,' and by his saying 'I do not know whether the disbeliever is in Paradise or Hell' or 'I do not know where the disbeliever will end up.' And he is killed for saying 'I curse the two schools' in response to 'Which of the two schools are you: Abu Hanifa or al-Shafi'i?' even if he repents, he is punished. And he becomes an apostate by his denying the origin of witr prayer and the sacrifice, and by his considering intercourse with a menstruating woman lawful, not by his saying 'I have not even a handspan in Paradise' due to underestimating his deeds, nor by his saying 'The recording angels do not write on this man,' nor by his saying 'This place has no god and no messenger' unless he intended to deny the religion, nor by the woman's saying 'I will not learn nor pray' in response to her husband's saying 'Learn,' nor by his denying the tithe or land tax, and he is not considered a sinner especially in this time, nor by his saying 'Whoever eats forbidden food has eaten what Allah provided him, but he sins.' And he becomes an apostate by his considering lawful something whose prohibition is known by necessity from the religion, without necessity, not by merely doing it without considering it lawful, contrary to what is transmitted from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding eating pork, and from Abu Hafs regarding wine, and the fatwa is on the first. And he becomes an apostate by his saying about something ugly that it is...
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage covers a wide range of additional causes of apostasy. Slandering Aisha (radiallahu anha) specifically (i.e., accusing her of adultery) is kufr because it challenges the Quranic revelation of her innocence. Denying the companionship (suhbah) of Abu Bakr is kufr because his companionship is established by the Quran ("ثاني اثنين"). Denying the caliphate of Abu Bakr or Umar is kufr according to the most correct view, since it rejects the consensus of the Companions. However, saying 'Were it not for our Prophet, Adam would not have been created' is a mistaken statement but not kufr. Conditional statements expressing refusal to obey Allah's commands (e.g., 'If God commanded me, I wouldn't do it') are clearly kufr because they imply rebellion against Allah. Similarly, saying one would not accept Paradise if it meant being without a certain person, or if it were given for a particular deed, is kufr because it shows discontent with Allah's decree. Saying 'I will not abandon criticism for deferment' in reply to 'Leave this world for the hereafter' implies rejection of the afterlife. Saying one would not obey if commanded to give more zakat or fast more than prescribed is kufr as it challenges divine legislation. The statement 'Faith increases and decreases' is considered kufr by Hanafis because it implies that faith is created and changeable, whereas faith is the affirmation of the heart (tasdiq) which does not increase or decrease. Expressing ignorance about the final abode of disbelievers is also kufr because the Quran explicitly states they are in Hell. Cursing both Hanafi and Shafi'i schools (i.e., 'I curse the two schools') is punishable by death even after repentance because it mocks the scholars of Islam. Denying the witr prayer and the sacrifice (udhiyah) as part of the religion is kufr. Considering intercourse with a menstruating woman lawful is kufr because it violates a clear prohibition. On the other hand, some statements are not kufr, such as a woman refusing to learn or pray in response to her husband's command (since it may be out of laziness rather than denial), or denying the tithe ('ushr) or land tax (kharaj) in modern times because these are not universally established today. Saying 'Whoever eats haram has eaten what Allah provided but sins' is also not kufr because it acknowledges that even forbidden provision comes from Allah's creation. However, actually considering something haram as halal (istihlal) is kufr, whereas merely committing the act without believing it halal is not kufr, contrary to what Imam Muhammad reported about pork and Abu Hafs about wine; the fatwa is on the former (that istihlal is kufr). The passage ends abruptly with 'and he becomes an apostate by his saying about something ugly that it is...' indicating continuation.

Key Terms
الاستحلال (al-istihlal): Considering something forbidden (haram) to be lawful (halal)
إنكار الضروري (inkar al-daruri): Denying what is necessarily known of the religion
الوتر (al-witr): The witr prayer, which is wajib in the Hanafi school

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone says 'I do not know where the disbeliever will end up'?
A) It is kufr.
B) It is not kufr.
C) It is makruh tanzihi.
D) It is permissible.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy is caused by denying daruriyyat, practicing istihlal, or making statements that imply rebellion against Allah, while mere sinning without istihlal does not remove one from Islam.

Theological Dispute: Is Haram Considered Provision (Rizq)?
Commentary on a statement and refutation of Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of rizq, explain why it includes haram, and refute the Mu'tazila position using linguistic and theological arguments.

Core Idea
Rizq is whatever Allah provides, halal or haram; sin is on the acquisition, not the provision.

This lesson examines a theological dispute between Ahl al-Sunnah (including Hanafis) and the Mu'tazila over the definition of rizq (provision). The Mu'tazila restrict rizq to lawful property, denying that haram can be from Allah. The Hanafi position affirms that Allah provides all sustenance, whether halal or haram, but the servant is accountable for the means of acquisition. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a correct theology of divine provision and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate that according to Ahl al-Sunnah, rizq is whatever Allah directs to a living being, regardless of its lawful or unlawful nature.
This is based on Quranic usage: 'And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision' (Hud:6).
2
Identify the Mu'tazila objection
The Mu'tazila define rizq as property lawfully owned and consumed; therefore, haram cannot be rizq because it cannot be legitimately owned.
They rely on a definition that ties rizq to ownership and lawful acquisition.
3
Follow the Mu'tazila proof
Examine their reasoning: if haram were rizq, then Allah would be providing evil, which they consider impossible. Hence, haram is not rizq.
This stems from their theological principle that Allah cannot do evil.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between the provision itself (rizq) which is created by Allah and is not evil, and the sinful act of acquisition committed by the human. Haram food is still a created substance; the sin lies in the human's choice to obtain it unlawfully.
Allah's attribute of provision (ar-Razzaq) encompasses all creation; evil is attributed to human action, not to Allah's creation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If someone eats haram, Hanafis say he has consumed Allah's provision but commits a sin by the unlawful means. Mu'tazila say he has not consumed provision at all, contradicting the linguistic and Quranic understanding.
This affects one's view of divine sustenance and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا بقوله من أكل حراماً فقد أكل ما رزقه الله لكنه أثم الظاهر أن هذا الفرع مبني على رأي المعتزلة لأن الرزق عند أهل السنة ما يسوقه الله تعالى إلى الحيوان فيأكله، وعند الجمهور ما ينتفع به أكلاً أو لبساً أو غيرهما، وأن ذلك المنساق قد يكون حلالاً وقد يكون حراماً، وعند المعتزلة الحرام ليس برزق لأنهم فسروه بمملوك يأكله المالك ومبنى الاختلاف على أن الإضافة إلى الله تعالى: معتبرة في مفهوم الرزق وأنه لا رازق إلا الله تعالى وحده وأن العبد يستحق الذم والعقاب على أكل الحرام، وما يكون مستنداً إلى الله تعالى لا يكون قبيحاً ومرتكبه لا يستحق الذم بناء على أصلهم الفاسد وتمام مبحثه والجواب عنه مذكور في كتب العقائد فتأمل.
He said: (And not by his saying: Whoever eats haram has eaten what Allah provided him, but he is sinful.) It appears that this branch is built on the opinion of the Mu'tazila, because provision (rizq) according to Ahl al-Sunnah is what Allah directs to the animal and it eats, and according to the majority it is what is benefited from, by eating, wearing, or otherwise, and that which is brought may be halal or haram. According to the Mu'tazila, haram is not provision because they define it as property that the owner eats. The basis of the difference is that attribution to Allah is considered in the concept of rizq and that there is no provider except Allah alone, and that the servant deserves blame and punishment for eating haram, and what is attributable to Allah cannot be evil and its perpetrator does not deserve blame, based on their corrupt principle. The full discussion and its answer are mentioned in books of creed, so reflect.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from the matn: 'And not by his saying: Whoever eats haram has eaten what Allah provided him, but he is sinful.' The commentator explains that this statement seems to follow the Mu'tazila view, not the Sunni position. According to Ahl al-Sunnah, rizq (provision) is whatever Allah sends to a living being, whether halal or haram. The Mu'tazila define rizq as only that which is lawfully owned and consumed, so haram cannot be rizq. This disagreement stems from whether the term 'rizq' in Islamic theology includes haram. The author refutes the Mu'tazila position, noting that for more detail one should refer to books of creed (aqaid).

Key Terms
رزق (rizq): Anything that benefits a living being, provided by Allah, whether halal or haram.
معتزلة (Mu'tazila): A theological school that holds reason as primary; they deny that haram is rizq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of rizq (provision) for Ahl al-Sunnah?
A) Only that which is lawfully earned and consumed.
B) Whatever Allah directs to a living being, whether halal or haram.
C) Only that which is consumed in a halal manner.
D) Only the sustenance that leads to reward.

Key Takeaway
Rizq is defined by divine provision, not by human lawfulness; haram food is still rizq, but the eater is sinful.

Rulings on Denying Eschatological Matters
Rulings on disbelief in eschatological matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which denials of eschatological matters constitute apostasy in the Hanafi school and state the exception for ignorance.

Core Idea
Denial of core eschatological beliefs is kufr; ignorance may excuse, but only if taught.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists specific eschatological beliefs whose denial leads to apostasy. It also addresses a woman's ignorance and certain statements that may appear problematic but are not deemed kufr. Understanding these rulings is crucial for distinguishing between outright disbelief and mere misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the denials that constitute kufr
List the eschatological matters mentioned: Day of Judgment, resurrection, Paradise, Hell, Scale, Reckoning, Bridge, scrolls of deeds. Denial of any of these is kufr.
2
Note the exception for a specific individual
Denying the resurrection of a specific man (e.g., a particular person) does not make one an apostate, as such denial may stem from ignorance about that person.
This distinguishes general resurrection from personal.
3
Analyze the case of the ignorant woman
Abu Yusuf ruled that a woman who does not know that disbelievers will enter Hell is not an apostate; she should be taught. This shows that ignorance of a basic matter can excuse kufr if the person is teachable.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; some may disagree.
4
Examine non-kufr statements
The passage lists two statements that are NOT kufr: (1) 'Only the soul is rewarded and punished' and (2) 'I entrust it to the One who does not prevent the thief.' These may be misinterpretations or figurative expressions, not outright denial.
Context and intent matter.
5
Apply the ruling to additional denials
Denying the vision of Allah in Paradise and denying the punishment of the grave are explicitly kufr. Expressing uncertainty about whether Jews/Christians will be punished is also kufr, as it doubts clear texts.
Certainty is required in these matters.

وبإنكاره القيامة أو البعث أو الجنة أو النار أو الميزان أو الحساب أو الصراط أو الصحائف المكتوب فيها أعمال العباد لا إذا أنكر بعث رجل بعينه واختلف في تكفير امرأة لا تعرف أن اليهود يبعثون، وسئل أبو يوسف رحمه الله عن امرأة لا تعرف أن الكفار يدخلون النار فقال : تعلم ولا تكفر. ويكفر بإنكاره رؤية الله عز وجل بعد دخول الجنة وبإنكاره عذاب القبر وبقوله لا أعلم أن اليهود والنصارى إذا بعثوا هل يعذبون بالنار وبإنكار حشر بني آدم أو غيرهم، ولا بقوله إن المثاب والمعاقب الروح فقط ولا بقوله سلمتها إلى من لا يمنع السارق جواباً لمن وضع ثيابه وقال سلمتها إلى الله.
And by his denying the Day of Judgment, or resurrection, or Paradise, or Hell, or the Scale, or the Reckoning, or the Bridge, or the scrolls in which the deeds of servants are written, not if he denies the resurrection of a specific man. And there is disagreement about the apostasy of a woman who does not know that the Jews will be resurrected. And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, was asked about a woman who does not know that the disbelievers will enter Hell; he said: 'She should be taught and does not become an apostate.' And he becomes an apostate by denying the vision of Allah after entering Paradise, and by denying the punishment of the grave, and by his saying: 'I do not know whether the Jews and Christians, when they are resurrected, will be punished in Hell,' and by denying the gathering of human beings or others. And not by his saying: 'Only the soul is rewarded and punished,' and not by his saying: 'I entrust it to the One who does not prevent the thief' in response to one who placed his clothes and said 'I entrust them to Allah.'
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage continues listing matters that cause apostasy. Denial of any core eschatological belief—resurrection, Paradise, Hell, the Scale, etc.—is kufr. However, denying a specific person's resurrection (e.g., a particular individual) is not kufr, as it may be from ignorance. There is disagreement about a woman who is ignorant of basic eschatological facts; Abu Yusuf ruled that she should be taught, not declared apostate. Denying the vision of Allah in Paradise is kufr. Denying the punishment of the grave is kufr. Expressing uncertainty about whether disbelievers will be punished in Hell is also kufr, as it involves doubt in clear texts. The statement 'Only the soul is rewarded and punished' is not kufr, as it may stem from misunderstanding. The statement 'I entrust it to the One who does not prevent the thief' when entrusting clothes to Allah is not kufr; it is a figure of speech.

Key Terms
إنكار (inkar): Denial; rejecting a tenet of faith.
عذاب القبر (adhab al-qabr): Punishment of the grave; a matter of aqida.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Yusuf say about a woman who does not know that disbelievers will enter Hell?
A) She becomes an apostate immediately.
B) She should be taught and does not become an apostate.
C) She is exempt due to ignorance.
D) She is considered a hypocrite.

Key Takeaway
Denial of core eschatological beliefs is kufr, but ignorance and figurative speech may exempt a person from the ruling of apostasy.

Avoiding Takfir: The Hanafi Principle on Ambiguous Utterances
Compilation of rulings on specific verbal statements and their effect on apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between utterances that are clearly apostasy and those that are figurative or lack intent, applying the Hanafi principle of avoiding takfir.

Core Idea
An utterance is not apostasy if it can be interpreted figuratively or if the speaker lacked intent to mock religion.

This lesson examines a series of rulings from the Hanafi school on specific verbal statements and their impact on one's Islamic faith. The central principle is that takfir (declaring someone an apostate) is a grave matter and should be avoided whenever possible. Many statements that may seem problematic are interpreted in a favorable light, considering cultural expressions, figurative language, and the speaker's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance
Read each statement presented in the source and determine exactly what was said. Note any contextual details (e.g., to whom it was said, in what situation).
For example, 'I created this tree' is said by a Persian speaker.
2
Check for a plausible non-kufr interpretation
Apply the Hanafi principle that if the utterance can reasonably be interpreted in a way that does not reject Islam, it is not considered apostasy. Look for figurative meanings, cultural idioms, or the possibility that the speaker meant something else.
E.g., 'I am Pharaoh' is usually just a claim of power, not a statement of belief.
3
Assess the speaker's intent
Determine whether the speaker intended to mock religion, deny a fundamental, or simply used a figure of speech. Intent is crucial: if there is no intent to commit kufr, the ruling is lenient.
The text mentions 'قاصداً' (intending) in several places.
4
Apply the ruling
Based on the interpretation and intent, classify the utterance as either not causing apostasy (no takfir) or causing apostasy (takfir). If in doubt, avoid takfir.
The text explicitly states many utterances do NOT cause apostasy: e.g., 'I created this tree' (unless literal), 'I am Pharaoh', 'You should prostrate to me' (meaning gratitude).
5
Note any disagreement (ikhtilaf)
Be aware of points where Hanafi scholars differed, such as the case of saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills'. Recognize that the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is to avoid takfir in ambiguous cases.
The text says they differed on that phrase; the preferred view is that it is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير/ باب أحكام المرتدين
۲۰۹
وبعزمه على أن يأمر بالكفر، وبقوله لمن ينازعه افعل كل يوم عشرة أمثالك من الطين أو لم يقل من الطين قاصداً . من حيث الخلقة لا من حيث بيان ،صنعته ولا بقوله قد خلقت هذه الشجرة لأنه يراد به عادة الفرس حتى لو عنى به حقيقة الخلق يكفر، ولا بقوله لغيره ينبغي لك أن تسجد لي سجدة لأن المراد منه الشكر والمنة ويكفر بقوله أي شيء أصنع إذا لزمني الكفر جواباً لمن قال له أي شيء تصنع قد لزمك الكفر. وبإبداله حرفاً أو آية من القرآن عمداً، وباعتقاد أن الخراج ملك السلطان لا بقوله أنا فرعون أو إبليس إلا إذا قال اعتقادي كاعتقاد فرعون، ومن حسن كلام أهل الأهواء وقال معنوي أو كلام له معنى صحيح إن كان ذلك كفراً من القائل كفر المحسن، وكذا من حسن رسوم الكفرة واختلفوا في تكفير من قال إن إبراهيم بن أدهم رأوه بالبصرة يوم التروية وفي ذلك اليوم بمكة. ومسألة ثبوت النسب بين المشرقي وبين المغربية تؤيد القائل بعدمه ويخاف الكفر على من قال بحياتي وحياتك. وأجمعوا على أن من شك في إيمانه فهو كافر وهو أن يكون مصدقاً لكن يشك أن هذا التصديق إيمان أو كفر، واختلفوا في أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله. هذا كله حاصل ما في التتارخانية من الفصول من باب ألفاظ التكفير سوى الفارسي .
،
الله
مع ما
وفي الخلاصة : يكفر بقوله أنا بريء من الثواب والعقاب، وبقوله لو عاقبني بي من المرض ومشقة الولد فقد ظلمني وبشد المرأة حبلاً في وسطها وقالت هذا زنار ومن أبغض عاملاً. من غير سبب ظاهر خيف عليه الكفر، ولو صغر الفقيه أو العلوي قاصداً الاستخفاف بالدين كفر لا إن لم يقصده والسجود للجبابرة كفر إن أراد به العبادة لا إن أراد به التحية على قول الأكثر . وفي البزارية قال علماؤنا : من قال أرواح المشايخ حاضرة تعلم
يكفر،
(
، ومن قال بخلق القرآن فهو كافر، ومن قال إن الإيمان مخلوق فهو كافر؛ كذا في كثير من الفتاوى وهو محمول على بمعنى هداية الرب وأما فعل العبد فهو مخلوق . وإذا أخذ أحد المكس مقاطعة فقالوا له مبارك كفروا . ووقعت بسراي الجديدة واقعة وهي أن واحداً قاطع على مال معلوم احتساباً بها أعني الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر فضربوا على بابه طبولات وبوقات ونادوا مبارك باد لمقاطعته الاحتساب وكان إمام الجامع الصلاة فامتنعنا من عرض على نفسه الإسلام أخذاً من هذه المسألة قال لرجل يا أحمر قال خلقني الله من سويق التفاح وخلقك من طين كفر قال واحد من الفسقة لو وضعت هذه الخمرة بين يدي جبريل عليه السلام لرفعها على جناحه يكفر، ولا يكفر بقوله يا حاضر یا ناظر ولا بقوله درویش درویشان والقول بالكفر بكل منهما باطل وفي جامع الفصولين روى الطحاوي عن أصحابنا : لا يخرج الرجل من الإيمان إلا جحود ما أدخله فيه، ثم ما تيقن أنه خلفه حتى منه فهذا لا يكون كفراً، وقد عثرنا على رواية أبي حنيفة أن الرضا بكفر الغير كفر من غير تفصيل .
Book of Siyar / Chapter of Rulings on Apostates. And [he does not become an apostate] by his resolve to command disbelief, nor by his saying to one who disputes with him: 'Do every day ten times the like of you from clay' - whether he said 'from clay' or not, intending it from the perspective of creation, not from the perspective of describing his craftsmanship. Nor by his saying: 'I have created this tree', because it is customarily meant by the Persians; but if he meant the literal creation, he disbelieves. Nor by his saying to someone else: 'You should prostrate to me once', because what is meant is gratitude and favor. And he disbelieves by his saying: 'What shall I do if disbelief is incumbent upon me?' as an answer to one who said to him: 'What do you do? Disbelief has become incumbent upon you.' And by his deliberately replacing a letter or verse of the Qur'an. And by his belief that the kharaj tax is the property of the sultan. He does not disbelieve by his saying: 'I am Pharaoh' or 'I am Iblis', unless he says: 'My belief is like the belief of Pharaoh.' And whoever praises the speech of the people of innovation, and says it has meaning or is speech with correct meaning - if that [speech] is disbelief from the speaker, then the one who praised it disbelieves. Similarly, whoever praises the customs of disbelievers. And they differed regarding the takfir of one who said: 'Ibrahim ibn Adham was seen in Basra on the day of Tarwiyah and on that same day in Mecca.' And the issue of establishing lineage between an Easterner and a Westerner supports the one who says it is not established, and one fears disbelief for one who says: 'By my life and your life.' And they agreed that whoever doubts his faith is a disbeliever - that is, one who is affirming but doubts whether this affirmation is faith or disbelief. And they differed regarding [the phrase] 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' All this is the summary of what is in al-Tatarkhaniyya from the chapters of the Chapter of Utterances of Takfir, except for the Persian [section]. And in al-Khulasa: He disbelieves by his saying: 'I am free from reward and punishment.' And by his saying: 'If He punishes me with illness and hardship of childbirth, He has wronged me.' And by a woman tying a rope around her waist and saying: 'This is a zunnar.' And whoever hates a worker without apparent reason, one fears disbelief for him. And if a faqih or an Alawi belittles [someone] intending to slight the religion, he disbelieves; if he did not intend it, he does not disbelieve. And prostrating to tyrants is disbelief if he intended worship, but not if he intended greeting, according to the majority. And in al-Bazzaziyya: Our scholars said: Whoever says that the spirits of the saints are present and know, disbelieves. And whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever. And whoever says that faith is created is a disbeliever; thus in many fatwas, and it is interpreted as meaning the guidance of the Lord, but the act of the servant is created. And if a tax collector takes a lump sum and they say to him 'Mubarak', they disbelieve. And an incident occurred in Saray al-Jadida: a person contracted for a fixed amount for hisba (enjoining good and forbidding evil), and they beat drums and trumpets at his door and proclaimed 'Mubarak bad' for his hisba contract. And the imam of the mosque was praying, so we refrained from presenting [the matter] to him, taking from this issue. He said to a man: 'O red one!' He said: 'Allah created me from apple porridge and created you from clay.' He disbelieves. One of the corrupt said: 'If this wine were placed before Jibril, peace be upon him, he would raise it with his wing.' He disbelieves. And he does not disbelieve by his saying: 'O present one, O watcher', nor by his saying: 'Darwish, darwishes', and the claim of disbelief in each of them is false. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Tahawi narrated from our companions: 'A man does not leave faith except by rejecting what brought him into it. Then what he is certain of after that does not become disbelief.' And we have come across a narration from Abu Hanifa that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief without distinction.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings from multiple Hanafi sources (al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, Jami' al-Fusulayn) concerning specific utterances and their effect on apostasy. The author, Ibn Nujaym, collects rulings to guide the mufti on when to pronounce takfir and when to avoid it. The overall principle is that apostasy requires a clear verbal denial of fundamentals or an explicit intention to mock religion; many statements that might seem problematic are interpreted in a favorable light to avoid takfir. For example, saying 'I created this tree' is not kufr if understood as a Persian expression for 'I made', but if literal creation is intended, it is kufr. Similarly, claiming to be Pharaoh or Iblis is not automatically kufr unless one affirms their beliefs. The passage also includes rulings on praising heretical speech, customs of disbelievers, doubting one's faith, and specific modern incidents. The Hanafi school emphasizes that takfir is a severe matter and should be avoided when possible; hence many utterances are deemed not to constitute apostasy unless clear intent to reject Islam is present.

Key Terms
الرضا بكفر الغير (al-rida bi kufr al-ghayr): Being pleased with another person's disbelief
الاستخفاف بالدين (al-istikhfaf bi al-din): Belittling or showing contempt for religion
الشك في الإيمان (al-shakk fi al-iman): Doubting whether one's own faith is true

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following utterances is NOT considered apostasy according to the Hanafi school, based on this lesson?
A) Saying 'I have created this tree' intending literal creation
B) Saying 'I am Pharaoh' with the belief that one's creed is like Pharaoh's
C) Saying 'You should prostrate to me' meaning gratitude
D) Saying 'What shall I do if disbelief is incumbent upon me?'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school avoids takfir for utterances that have a plausible non-kufr interpretation or lack intent to reject Islam.

Clear Utterances of Apostasy and the Principle of Certainty
Compilation of rulings on specific utterances that clearly cause apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify specific utterances that constitute clear apostasy and apply the Hanafi principle that a person remains Muslim unless they explicitly reject a fundamental of Islam.

Core Idea
Clear denial of reward and punishment or explicit mockery of religion is apostasy, but the default remains the preservation of faith.

This lesson continues the compilation of rulings on utterances that entail apostasy, drawing from al-Khulasa, al-Bazzariyya, and other sources. It presents statements that are unequivocally kufr, such as denying reward and punishment, accusing Allah of injustice, and mocking religion. The lesson also introduces the important maxim from al-Tahawi: a person only leaves Islam by rejecting what brought them into it, and subsequent matters of doubt do not cause kufr. This principle reinforces the Hanafi tendency to avoid takfir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance
Read each statement from the source. Note if it contains explicit denial of Islamic fundamentals, mockery, or attribution of imperfection to Allah.
E.g., 'I am free from reward and punishment' denies the afterlife.
2
Assess the statement's impact on fundamentals
Determine whether the statement directly contradicts a known essential of Islam (e.g., existence of Allah, prophethood, afterlife, justice of Allah).
Accusing Allah of injustice is a direct contradiction.
3
Check for exceptions or differences
Some statements have nuances. For example, prostrating to tyrants is kufr only if intended as worship, not greeting. Also, some cases have ikhtilaf among scholars.
The text says 'السجود للجبابرة كفر إن أراد به العبادة لا إن أراد به التحية'.
4
Apply the ruling and consider the default
If the utterance clearly constitutes kufr, the ruling is apostasy. However, if there is any doubt, the default is to keep the person within Islam, as per the maxim: 'A man does not leave faith except by rejecting what brought him into it.'
The final maxim from al-Tahawi is key.
5
Understand the intra-Hanafi difference on al-rida bi kufr al-ghayr
Be aware that Abu Hanifa's narration states that being pleased with another's disbelief is kufr, while later scholars may distinguish. The mufta bihi is to avoid takfir in ambiguous situations.
See the last line of the passage.

And [he does not become an apostate] by his resolve to command disbelief, nor by his saying to one who disputes with him: 'Do every day ten times the like of you from clay' - whether he said 'from clay' or not, intending it from the perspective of creation, not from the perspective of describing his craftsmanship. And whoever praises the speech of the people of innovation, and says it has meaning or is speech with correct meaning - if that [speech] is disbelief from the speaker, then the one who praised it disbelieves. Similarly, whoever praises the customs of disbelievers. And they differed regarding the takfir of one who said: 'Ibrahim ibn Adham was seen in Basra on the day of Tarwiyah and on that same day in Mecca.' And the issue of establishing lineage between an Easterner and a Westerner supports the one who says it is not established, and one fears disbelief for one who says: 'By my life and your life.' And they agreed that whoever doubts his faith is a disbeliever - that is, one who is affirming but doubts whether this affirmation is faith or disbelief. And they differed regarding [the phrase] 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' All this is the summary of what is in al-Tatarkhaniyya from the chapters of the Chapter of Utterances of Takfir, except for the Persian [section]. And in al-Khulasa: He disbelieves by his saying: 'I am free from reward and punishment.' And by his saying: 'If He punishes me with illness and hardship of childbirth, He has wronged me.' And by a woman tying a rope around her waist and saying: 'This is a zunnar.' And whoever hates a worker without apparent reason, one fears disbelief for him. And if a faqih or an Alawi belittles [someone] intending to slight the religion, he disbelieves; if he did not intend it, he does not disbelieve. And prostrating to tyrants is disbelief if he intended worship, but not if he intended greeting, according to the majority. And in al-Bazzaziyya: Our scholars said: Whoever says that the spirits of the saints are present and know, disbelieves. And whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever. And whoever says that faith is created is a disbeliever; thus in many fatwas, and it is interpreted as meaning the guidance of the Lord, but the act of the servant is created. And if a tax collector takes a lump sum and they say to him 'Mubarak', they disbelieve. And an incident occurred in Saray al-Jadida: a person contracted for a fixed amount for hisba (enjoining good and forbidding evil), and they beat drums and trumpets at his door and proclaimed 'Mubarak bad' for his hisba contract. And the imam of the mosque was praying, so we refrained from presenting [the matter] to him, taking from this issue. He said to a man: 'O red one!' He said: 'Allah created me from apple porridge and created you from clay.' He disbelieves. One of the corrupt said: 'If this wine were placed before Jibril, peace be upon him, he would raise it with his wing.' He disbelieves. And he does not disbelieve by his saying: 'O present one, O watcher', nor by his saying: 'Darwish, darwishes', and the claim of disbelief in each of them is false. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Tahawi narrated from our companions: 'A man does not leave faith except by rejecting what brought him into it. Then what he is certain of after that does not become disbelief.' And we have come across a narration from Abu Hanifa that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief without distinction.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings from multiple Hanafi sources (al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, Jami' al-Fusulayn) concerning specific utterances and their effect on apostasy. The author, Ibn Nujaym, collects rulings to guide the mufti on when to pronounce takfir and when to avoid it. The overall principle is that apostasy requires a clear verbal denial of fundamentals or an explicit intention to mock religion; many statements that might seem problematic are interpreted in a favorable light to avoid takfir. For example, saying 'I created this tree' is not kufr if understood as a Persian expression for 'I made', but if literal creation is intended, it is kufr. Similarly, claiming to be Pharaoh or Iblis is not automatically kufr unless one affirms their beliefs. The passage also includes rulings on praising heretical speech, customs of disbelievers, doubting one's faith, and specific modern incidents. The Hanafi school emphasizes that takfir is a severe matter and should be avoided when possible; hence many utterances are deemed not to constitute apostasy unless clear intent to reject Islam is present.

Key Terms
الرضا بكفر الغير (al-rida bi kufr al-ghayr): Being pleased with another person's disbelief
الاستخفاف بالدين (al-istikhfaf bi al-din): Belittling or showing contempt for religion
الشك في الإيمان (al-shakk fi al-iman): Doubting whether one's own faith is true

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Tahawi, what is the condition for a person to leave Islam (apostasy)?
A) Committing any sin
B) Rejecting what brought him into Islam (i.e., the fundamentals)
C) Doubting some matters after being certain
D) Being pleased with another's disbelief

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes that apostasy requires clear and intentional rejection of Islamic fundamentals; ambiguous statements or doubts do not automatically remove one from the faith.

Principles of Takfir and Procedure for the Apostate
Explanation of principles of takfir and the apostate procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of avoiding takfir when possible and state the three-day procedure for an apostate, including the ruling on presenting Islam.

Core Idea
Takfir is only for clear, intentional rejection; doubts must be resolved in favor of the Muslim.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq sets out the foundational Hanafi framework for dealing with apostasy. It begins with the key principle that established Islam is not removed by doubt, and then details the procedure for handling an apostate: presenting Islam, clarifying doubts, and a three-day grace period. The author, Ibn Nujaym, emphasizes restraint in declaring takfir and provides a hierarchy of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational principle
The first sentence establishes that if there is any doubt about whether an act is apostasy, the ruling remains non-kufr. This overrides all other considerations.
Islam is exalted; established faith is not removed by doubt.
2
Apply the principle to the mufti’s methodology
When an issue has multiple aspects pointing to takfir and one aspect preventing it, the mufti must incline towards the aspect that prevents takfir, to think well of the Muslim.
Exception: if the person explicitly intends the meaning that necessitates kufr.
3
Categorize the four types of utterances
The passage categorizes uttering kufr words into: joking/playing, mistake/compulsion, knowing/deliberate, and voluntary with ignorance. Each has a different ruling on apostasy.
Joking makes one an apostate; mistake/compulsion does not; knowing/deliberate does; ignorant is disputed.
4
Identify the procedure for an apostate
After apostasy is confirmed, the imam or judge presents Islam to the apostate (mustahabb, not wajib), clarifies any doubts, and imprisons him for three days. If he repents, he is freed; otherwise he is executed.
The presentation is recommended according to the apparent school because the call has already reached him.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on respite
There is a difference on whether the three-day deferment is given automatically or only if the apostate requests it. The apparent narration from al-Jami' al-Saghir is that he is killed immediately unless he asks for respite.
Ibn Nujaym prefers the view that gives automatic respite to maximize chance of return.

Source Text
